<div id="review_1648743082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648743082" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648743082?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648743082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8094722466126984352">**UPDATE 10/21/18: Yes, rereading this already.....**<br/><br/><br/>**UPDATE: Because ever since I read this book it has completely wrecked me from making significant progress on anything else. It's the sign of a great book when a month and three other books can pass, and your mind is still trapped by this one. Read at your own risk 😭😭😭😭.**<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449203344ra/17250996.gif' width='' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The question is not whether you will love, hurt, dream, and die. It is what you will love, why you will hurt, when you will dream, and how you will die. This is you</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8094722466126984352" style="display:none">**UPDATE 10/21/18: Yes, rereading this already.....**<br><br><br>**UPDATE: Because ever since I read this book it has completely wrecked me from making significant progress on anything else. It's the sign of a great book when a month and three other books can pass, and your mind is still trapped by this one. Read at your own risk 😭😭😭😭.**<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449203344ra/17250996.gif" width="" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The question is not whether you will love, hurt, dream, and die. It is what you will love, why you will hurt, when you will dream, and how you will die. This is your choice. You cannot pick the destination, only the path.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <u>A Full Five Stars: ✰✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br><br>So here's the thing - I'm a slow reader, and also a slow writer, so this review is coming behind a myriad of other reviews singing this book's praises. I’ve almost been hesitant to even write a review because of that. I can't say anything beyond what has already been said - <b>mainly, that this book is simply outstanding</b>, surpassing my expectations and more. <br><br>But I can talk about why this book was special and significant to me personally. Really - seriously - this book was amazing, in so many different ways, but it's not just the great world building, epic plot, and compelling characters that would make me recommend this book or this series. <b>I will recommend <i>The Stormlight Archive</i> to literally everybody I know because of the impact it has made on me personally</b>, and that’s not something I can convey in a five star rating or by talking about what I think is really the artistic genius of Brandon Sanderson. <br><br>Each of these books was released at a time in my life when I was going through some huge transition phases, and times of confusion in a lot of ways. Including this book. It's actually a little creepy haha. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings__The_Stormlight_Archive___1_" title="The Way of Kings (The Stormlight Archive, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a> came out when I was fourteen, dealing with insecurity, isolation, and major depression. I didn't have any friends, because nobody liked me - and I couldn't blame them - but I wanted to change, and this time of my life was hugely formative because of that. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17332218.Words_of_Radiance__The_Stormlight_Archive___2_" title="Words of Radiance (The Stormlight Archive, #2) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a> came out when I was 17 and starting out in the career I have now (insurance sales), while finishing my degree online - which was completely daunting to me at the time. I remember being in one of my insurance classes, reading my huge hard cover of Words of Radiance during every break that we had, and it took me literally two months to finish it because I was still taking my regular online classes as well.<br><br>And then there's this book. I'm now 21, and I (at least I think) have become an emotionally healthy person haha; I have loads of experience in a career I've managed to make work, am married to my best friend, and we now have a baby on the way, which has brought about another huge transition phase for us. <br><br>I hold really unique emotional ties to a lot of the characters in these books, and even certain aspects of the story, that I've never felt before with any other book series. Reading about Kaladin coming to terms with past hurt, and dealing with his pain and depression in the present, was always something that encouraged me. I needed those kinds of reminders - that it's possible to overcome, even after being brought so low. Reading Shallan's story helped me as I was fighting to become somebody better than who I was. It reminded me that the only way we can become the person we're supposed to be is by admitting to the wrongs of our past, accepting even the painful things of life, and then learning to truly confront it, rather than push it under the surface. Because <b>sometimes it's okay to hurt.</b><br><br>Reading about Dalinar, in a different sense, made me so thankful for redemption. That we are not defined simply by who we were, but by who we choose to be: <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sometimes a hypocrite is nothing more than a man in the process of changing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I can't really even put into words why these things are so meaningful to me. Even just putting the books aside, these are lessons that have worked their way into the heart of who I am as a person, and finding a book (or a series) that resonates with me like this just doesn't happen. I don't want to give away any spoilers, but this book in particular added A LOT, not just to the incredible story, but also to the themes that were previously developed in the first two books. <b>This will probably always be my favorite series of all time because of this.</b><br><br>*cough* Okay, now that my emotional dump is finished, I'll say a few more technical things about this book. <br><br>Normally I'd have a bunch of quotes in my review, but there were SO MANY GOOD QUOTES that were unfortunately also minor spoilers, so I didn't want to include anything that could be a potential giveaway. But this book surprised me. Sanderson took the story in a direction that I actually wasn't expecting, with a lot more tension, a whole lot of blood and brutality, and plenty of twists and turns along the way. <b>This was by far the most intense book yet in this series</b>. <br><br>The characters were developed even more fully than the prior books, with a spotlight on Dalinar and flashbacks into his life. Honestly, my favorite POV from this book was Bridge Four. Getting a little glimpse from the POV of several of my favorite characters from Bridge Four was awesome, and I only wish we would have had a little bit more than what we got. <br><br>The worldbuilding, as always, was top notch. This is Sanderson's masterpiece in this regard, and it just keeps getting better with each and every book.<br><br><b>
  <u>In Conclusion:</u>
</b><br><br>You'll hear a lot of people saying that "this book was better than the first two" or "this book wasn't as good as the first two", and while I can understand where those people are coming from, each of these books is different enough that it's extremely hard to compare them. All three of them sit pretty equally with me because of that, and the quality of the writing, worldbuilding, and character development never varies at all. <br><br><b>This is Sanderson at his best</b>. If you have not yet started this series, I literally can't emphasize enough how highly I recommend them. If you have read the first two books but have reservations about book number three - fear not haha. You will not be disappointed. <br><br>Happy reading =].</span>
  <a data-text-id="8094722466126984352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2162157236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162157236" />
    <a title="Helen 2.0" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0"><img alt="Helen 2.0" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460553725p2/39575951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2162157236?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575093348" href="/book/show/17250961-oathbringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=brs-done">brs-done</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=read-17">read-17</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=antihero">antihero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=hype-train">hype-train</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=original">original</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2162157236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10008714992889334862"><blockquote>
  <i>"Having power is a terrible burden, the worst thing imaginable, except for every other alternative."</i>
</blockquote><br/>Power and its burden seems to be a major theme in Oathbringer, which features a number of exciting and frustrating developments in its 1200 pages. (The most frustrating revelation of all is the fact that we will be waiting until 2020 at least for the fourth installment.)<br/><br/>Every Stormlight Archive volume is a character study of a different Knight Radiant; first Kaladin, then Shallan, and now Dali</span>
  <span id="freeText10008714992889334862" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"Having power is a terrible burden, the worst thing imaginable, except for every other alternative."</i>
</blockquote><br>Power and its burden seems to be a major theme in Oathbringer, which features a number of exciting and frustrating developments in its 1200 pages. (The most frustrating revelation of all is the fact that we will be waiting until 2020 at least for the fourth installment.)<br><br>Every Stormlight Archive volume is a character study of a different Knight Radiant; first Kaladin, then Shallan, and now Dalinar. Oathbringer focuses heavily on Dalinar’s past as the Blackthorn and the violent history he’s tried to put behind him through discipline and honor. <blockquote>
  <i>"You stand where you do because of a brutal determination to do what had to be done. It is because of that trail of corpses that you have the luxury to uphold some lofty, nebulous code. Well, it might make you feel better about your past, but morality is not a thing you can simply doff to put on the helm of battle, then put back on when you’re done with the slaughter.”</i>
</blockquote> Branderson definitely did not hold back on Dalinar’s characterization, turning him into a tortured man with a frightening past. What’s more, constant flashbacks to the mind of the Blackthorn did not detract at all from Dalinar’s plotline in the present, as I sometimes felt was the case with Shallan in Words of Radiance.<br><br><br>Kaladin faces bigger challenges than ever before in this book; his Windrunner ideals are rocked badly when he once again faces that, in a war, you cannot protect everyone, even if both sides are right in some way. Although I thought he was pushed to the sidelines a little to broaden our perspective of Roshar; chapters that may have followed Kal were instead dedicated to Teft, Venli, Moash, Renarin, and other emerging players on the field. Still, Kaladin gets some great lines, like: <blockquote>
<i>"Ten spears go to battle, and nine shatter. Did that war </i>forge<i> the one that remained? No. All the war did was identify the spear that would not break.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Mild spoilers in this paragraph only</b> – speaking of Kal, Oathbringer saw the unfortunate crash and burn of my favorite ship, Kallan. I was obviously disappointed, not so much that things didn’t pan out the way I would have liked, but rather that Branderson spent SO MUCH TIME building up their relationship in Words of Radiance that I ended book 3 feeling vaguely cheated. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513488814i/24693998._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Why set up a mutual attraction, both physical and emotional, between two characters then dismiss it offhand in a single chapter? From the hilarious scene where Kal and Shallan first met, through the entire chasmfiend fiasco, then all the little moments in Oathbringer when even Syl was shipping it – all casually pushed aside in a single scene. That felt kind of unfair. If the author was going to make Shallan endgame with someone else, there at least should have been more drama surrounding her final choice after all the buildup.<br><br><br>Overall, I liked that Oathbringer widened its focus a little more beyond the human scope and gave insight into the parshmen and spren worlds. In over 3000 pages of the series so far, things would have gotten old if we stuck with the same old characters. In book 4 I hope to read more from Lift, Venli, Jasnah, and Renarin.<br><br>Let me leave off with this fun little note Branderson may or may not have left to all his critics:<br> <blockquote>
  <i>"That a thing is hated is not proof that it’s great art, but the lack of hatred is certainly proof that it is not.”</i>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2876400415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2876400415" />
    <a title="Fares" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58818027-fares"><img alt="Fares" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581798339p2/58818027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2876400415?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fares" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fares" href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58818027-fares?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2876400415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4579472971125095376"><b>3.5 I guess.</b><br/><br/>Well if this isn't the biggest disappointment of the year then... Then I have some worrisome months ahead 😨<br/><br/>I would like to start this by apologizing to all the hardworking people that put a lot of time and effort into this book, I’m sorry I didn’t like this book as much as I hoped.<br/><br/>Before I start you should know that I love this series, that I went in with high expectations and that I been meaning to read this for the last 8 months. It’s always amazing to be back to this world and I l</span>
  <span id="freeText4579472971125095376" style="display:none"><b>3.5 I guess.</b><br /><br />Well if this isn't the biggest disappointment of the year then... Then I have some worrisome months ahead 😨<br /><br />I would like to start this by apologizing to all the hardworking people that put a lot of time and effort into this book, I’m sorry I didn’t like this book as much as I hoped.<br /><br />Before I start you should know that I love this series, that I went in with high expectations and that I been meaning to read this for the last 8 months. It’s always amazing to be back to this world and I love how I forget myself in it.<br />I love the writing and the characters and the plot, I love how the reveals are subtle and the endings are explosive. All this was amazing in the previous 2 books and some of it still holds in the third book. But it’s not the same, this book is just different, and not in a good way.<br /><br />If I must give just one reason it’d be this, I think Sanderson spread himself too thin with this one, I think he tried to do many things and incorporate too many Cosmere books and references but unfortunately, that meant he sacrificed a lot of the things I love. <br /><br />There’s a lot of small reasons why I didn’t enjoy this rather than just one big reason tho. It’s the pacing of the book, it’s the choices that I don’t understand why they have been made, it’s what I hoped for vs what I got and it’s what I hated in book 2 made bigger and worse this time.<br /><br />So I’ll start with the end of Words of Radiance. After finishing that book I made a tiny list (and by that I mean a list of 2 things) of what I hope to see in Oathbringer, not only did I not get what I want I kinda got the opposite and the things I hated in WoR were even more detailed in this one.<br /><br /><b>The first thing on the list was Renarin.</b> I loved him in WoR I wanted more of him and more than that, I wanted a good character development, one that only Sanderson could do. Not only Renarin was absolutely ignored but at the end his character changed so abruptly that I actually had to stop to wonder if this really happening (again not in a good way), why was that? Who came up with the idea to only give him a few pages at the end? I have no idea. Now maybe Renarin gets his own book in the future, maybe he even saves the world and becomes emperor, who knows? But I still didn’t get my Renarin chapters and I didn’t like what happened at the end with him.<br />What makes this worse is that other minor characters got their own chapters and not to mention the interludes that go into random characters in some random place, I like the interludes, but I won’t sacrifice Renarin for them.<br /><br />To be honest I don’t know if I hate what happened with him more or what happened with Moash and Teft, I really really would’ve loved if Renarin and Moash switched places, I do not mean plot-wise but the time devoted to their characters, I think I would’ve preferred to see Renarin’s character slowly developing and Moash coming out of nowhere and doing what he did. Unfortunately, that wasn’t the case and I ended up hating both, the one I liked got no scenes and the one I didn’t care much about got scenes but the change was rushed and didn’t feel real to me.<br /><br /><b>The second thing on the list was Elhokar.</b> After WoR I thought we’d get the character development of the ages, maybe that was unrealistic of me but something about Elhokar succeeding just felt right and for once in fantasy I hoped that the (somewhat) bad king actually gets a redeeming arc and learn from his mistakes. I won’t say anything more to not spoil you, I just didn’t like Elhokar’s development and found it very cheap.<br /><br />The things I didn’t like from book 2 that were even worse in this book are.<br /><br /><b>Shallan, Adolin and Kaladin.</b> I DO NOT like love triangles, especially and most importantly useless stupid ones! Yes I get that characters have feelings, yes sometimes it’s good to explore more about what would these characters do if such and such happens, all that is fine, however 2 things I absolutely do not agree with, one is a character that romanticizes cheating, and the other is a character realizes that there’s a relationship between two and ignores it bc well he’s in love and that’s all the excuse they need to act upon their feelings. Thank goodness the first one didn’t happen or else I’ll be writing an entirely different review. The second one did happen tho and it’s THE ABSOLUTE WORSE when your favorite, and I mean bestest characters in the series! Use that as an excuse to start a stupid romance with a stupid character nevertheless.<br />Anyway, I’m just glad it wasn’t as bad as it could’ve been.<br /><br />I also didn’t like Dalinar and Navani in book 2 and that continued to the beginning of this one but at the end I was too mad at the other romance to care for this and I actually got over it once they worked that issue.<br /><br /><b>The other thing I didn’t like about WoR is that it was too long.</b> Well technically I do like that it’s long it’s part of the fun of it and the writing is great to forget yourself in it but yeah there were moments were I just didn’t care about who’s talking or what’s happening, this was even more so in Oathbringer, some parts were just insignificant considering what happens at the end, literally the end of the world is coming soon but the actions of these characters doesn’t sound like they are really trying to prevent it, I mean the enemy is mobilizing forces and gathering supply and numbers but all Dalinar does is send one guy to scout, then send a small group to retake a city and he keeps chatting with other nations that don’t want to talk to him. I was comparing this to Empire of Storms in the sense that both were trying to get nations on their side and gather armies, and EoS did a better job imo, it did an even better job considering we had glimpses to what the enemy was trying to do unlike here which kept that info hidden till nearing the end.<br />I get that Dalinar isn’t into politics and he really was trying but come on dude, you have a guy that can literally fly why were you insisting that they come to you, you could’ve went to them, and his solution to that problem was one of the things I thought about from the very first chapters!<br /><br />This makes me want to talk about these characters and how at times they were kinda stupid if I’m being honest. <b>Here are some points I had problems with.</b><br /><br />-Relain, no one asked him about the parshmen and we didn’t hear from him after that one time at the beginning, maybe he knows nothing but guess what? You know less than nothing so every information he gives you is important.<br />-(WoR spoiler here) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jasnah  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>knows about Shadesmar and it’s a freakin entire world but no let’s not ask the thousand years old spren there. The group didn’t do that either.<br />-Some things are just too convenient, like Shallan’s weaving doesn’t draw the voidbringers but Kaladin does (hopefully this would be explained in the nest books)<br />-Dalinar and everyone really just takes what the stormfather says even tho he’s a shadow of a spren and half his memories are gone. There are books, read them and do your research! <br />-No one thought of asking the Shin people even tho the assassin was from there!<br />-The secret societies in this world, you idiots know they know something so why not seek them or infiltrate them!<br /><br />Also I had a huge problem with Kaladin in this book, I love him and maybe this is why I’m hard on him but my gosh can he be annoying at times, I mean I get it you want to save everyone, that’s great and I love you for it, but you also CAN’T SAVE EVERYONE! People will die! I liked his struggle in book 1 and even more so in book 2, but now it just feels like he’s repeating the same thing, maybe you should do what your father said and become a surgeon if you don’t know who to fight. After 3 long books I was hoping he’s over that now, especially that he gets attached too easily to people and it was unrealistic what he’s trying to do.<br /><br /><b>What disappointed me most tho is</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ there are no significant deaths in this series so far! I actually started hoping Odium takes Dalinar, I was rooting for the bad guys and I even wanted Kaladin to lose someone he cares for to see how his character takes it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As I mentioned before the pacing of this book was off for me, I like that these books end with explosive endings but this one felt forced. I think for me it felt like that bc as I said the character's focus was on so many things at the start and suddenly at the end everything is concentrated on one place.<br />I do not understand why somethings were handled the way they have been, I mainly mean the investigation Adolin was handed but also Kaladin visiting his family and leaving like that, Shallan and her brothers were never mentioned until the very end, and I thought Ialai's character was SO weak in this one compared to the other two books, both her and Amaram. I thought for sure they'd have a bigger role and present some problems for Dalinar but he managed to do that all in his own, they actually kinda helped him by not asking more about the investigation and just accepted what he gave them.<br /><br />Lastly what I hope is the next books explain more about some of the things that just don't make sense, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like how Dalinar basically faced a god and won! He literally holds worlds in his hands now! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I believe that’s all. The potential in this series was high and still is but I’d be lying if I don’t say that it took a plunge with this book, I mean this was on top of my all time favorite high fantasy books, now tho I don’t know if it can be on the top 5, and the problem is that I’m thinking of series that I never read but I’m sure would be better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4579472971125095376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2485412719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2485412719" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576550045p2/33359750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2485412719?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34039808-oathbringer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33359750-lisa?shelf=library-e-book">library-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2485412719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13004320231949158799">Man, oh man! Did I love this book? Yep! Much more than I was expecting. After "Word's of Radiance," I had a feeling this book wouldn't be as awesome. Silly me. It was just as good, but in a different way. I often underestimate Mr. Sandersons sense of humor. I'll have read a few hundred pages, and maybe giggle a bit,"in my head." Suddenly, for the next couple hundred pages I'm smiling and laughing, and oddly happy. These characters do tend to become so close to me that when I fall asleep reading,</span>
  <span id="freeText13004320231949158799" style="display:none">Man, oh man! Did I love this book? Yep! Much more than I was expecting. After "Word's of Radiance," I had a feeling this book wouldn't be as awesome. Silly me. It was just as good, but in a different way. I often underestimate Mr. Sandersons sense of humor. I'll have read a few hundred pages, and maybe giggle a bit,"in my head." Suddenly, for the next couple hundred pages I'm smiling and laughing, and oddly happy. These characters do tend to become so close to me that when I fall asleep reading, they all come into my dreams. Especially the Spren. I've woken myself up talking to those Spren! Seriously, if I'm lying I'm dying. I love Adolin for being exactly the good man he seems. Adolin really is the knight in shining armor/Shard. Except he's not a bloodthirsty butthole. Jasnah, for her completeness. She has awesome abilities, but she's strong and sure. Kal, is someone who I'm waiting for. To develop, I mean. He may be the best thing ever, but we'll see. I fly in my dreams, so of course I'm going to have a soft spot for anyone who can sort of fly! Shallan? Love her. What a mess! Dalinar.....Ah, Dalinar has my heart and soul. Dalinar's flashbacks were hard to see, but that is what made him. Dalinar is my King Arthur...and who doesn't need an Arthur? Still, through this whole 1249 page book, my heart jittered and jived when Bridge four took the stage."Page?" This is when Sanderson really shows off his humor! All these books need more of Bridge four. They show how humans can overcome the worst of themselves, and all that surrounds them...With a crackpot humor! The major revelation in this book wasn't such a shocker as it should have been. The main problem is that now all my questions have doubled. Eh, well! I hear the next book, #4 is due in 2020. Yikes! Just doing the math, if a new book comes out every 3 to 4 years, and from 2020 on we still have 6 books to go.....argh! I will be way into my seventies. Shhesh! Still, really what the hell, I'm sure I'll still be waiting around for George R.R. Martin to finish his next book in The Game of Thrones! "Yes, the same one we've been waiting 6,7,8,9?? Been so long, I can't recall.This book and series is well worth my time. 1249 pages does seem to fly by once you get lost in the tale. BTW....I really need a spren. Not the superpower spren, but just everyday spren. How cool would that be? Pattern would be great too!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13004320231949158799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2196861278" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196861278" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196861278?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=review-freebie">review-freebie</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196861278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16166715594634725675">Originally reviewed at <a href='https://bookwraiths.com/2017/11/27/oathbringer/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a>.<br/><br/>Having recently finished a binge read of the first three novels in <i>The Stormlight Archive</i>, I can honestly say my mind is filled with this intricately detailed, amazingly epic story, so much so that I am finding it difficult to put into words my feelings for this series and, specifically, its third installment: <i>Oathbringer</i>. Mainly, this is due to the distinct originality and uniqueness of this book, which is hard to adequately describe. The world of Roshar far d</span>
  <span id="freeText16166715594634725675" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="https://bookwraiths.com/2017/11/27/oathbringer/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a>.<br /><br />Having recently finished a binge read of the first three novels in <i>The Stormlight Archive</i>, I can honestly say my mind is filled with this intricately detailed, amazingly epic story, so much so that I am finding it difficult to put into words my feelings for this series and, specifically, its third installment: <i>Oathbringer</i>. Mainly, this is due to the distinct originality and uniqueness of this book, which is hard to adequately describe. The world of Roshar far different from Tolkien’s LoTR, Martin’s ASoIF, or even Jordan’s WoT yet still terribly familiar. Roshar’s characters seemingly the normal standard bearers of legendary epics until Brandon Sanderson’s molds them into very different configurations. The plot here following the tried-and-true fantasy tropes only to turn them upside down, sending a reader flailing about in delightful ignorance of what is coming next. And due to all this, I believe the best way for me to summarize my feelings about <i>Oathbringer</i> is to merely say it is one of the most magnificent fantasy books I’ve ever read and leave it at that.<br /><br />For those unfamiliar with ,<i>The Stormlight Archive</i>, it – like so many epic fantasy series – is centered upon the coming end of the world, as the cyclical Desolation Event comes upon the world of Roshar once again. The heralds of this cataclysm (the Voidbringers) having appeared along with the forces of Odium, and our band of “heroes” called upon to somehow, someway hold back the end of the world. Dalinar Kholin, Kaladin the Stormblessed, Shallan Davar, and Adolin Kholin finding themselves in far over their heads, no matter their pedigree and experience.<br /><br />Where <i>The Way of Kings</i> was centered upon Kaladin and <i>Words of Radiance</i> focused on Shallan, <i>Oathbringer</i>’s main character is Dalinar. This novel spending a great deal of time comparing and contrasting the Dalinar of the present with the Dalinar of the past. The honorable, noble and principled would-be savior of Roshar revealed to have been a far different, more ruthless individual in the past; this history going a long way in explaining the reaction of so many people to Dalinar’s attempts to make of them allies in his crusade against the Desolation.<br /><br />This focus on Dalinar does not mean the other characters of the series are left out in the cold however. In fact, Brandon Sanderson finds page time to weave compelling stories for Kaladin, Shallan, Adolin and many more. Each of these individuals dealing with new roles, emotional issues, and tough choices with long term repercussions. Some characters embrace their new identities, dealing with depression and addiction, but there are others who can’t or won’t, which causes them to have to deal with the pain of failure and fumble around to find other ways to change and grow as the world around them forces them to adapt to the evolving circumstances. All of this character development very raw, very real, and even more poignant and compelling due to this realism.<br /><br />As for the world building in <i>Oathbringer</i>, it is just as superb as you’d expect from Sanderson. The world of Roshar, its people, its places, and its secrets mesmerizing in the extreme. The author finding new twists to add to the mix, revealing even more epic places, and adding to the legends and lore of this immense world. There is even time spent continuing to evolve the nature of the Desolations, the Heralds, the Oathpact, and everything else touched upon in the tale up to this point, leaving readers with the firm assurance that there is still much they do not know about Roshar.<br /><br />Without a doubt, <i>Oathbringer</i> has raised the bar even higher for the already amazing ,<i>Stormlight Archive</i>, making me desperately wish I had the next installment of the series sitting before me so I could dive into its pages right now. Yes, there has been some tense moments, epic struggles, and riveting reveals in the series up to this point, and maybe I need a break from it, but I do not wish for one, since I know there is still a long ways to go before this ride ends and many more amazing things to come. So everyone out there who hasn’t read this series yet, trust me, it is time to go ahead and begin your reading journey with <i>The Stormlight Archive</i>, because you do not want to miss out on this epic fantasy masterpiece!<br /><br />I received this book from the publisher in exchange for a fair and honest review. I’d like to thank them for allowing me to receive this review copy and inform everyone that the review you have read is my opinion alone.</span>

</a>

    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hk7UgTR6dROIFfam0exLumyBIk1X0rIRzOZzWoQwgfBbs7bWkLtpEzFXwEySgFjgVB9i4BsCer8J4lho+b96jA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sY0iknI95T89nHDEZ80zCX4gThx2PTzaNmJoQX9el5dscEDF1vz5P4TeRi4koSBTRr4OsTrt9HTzZkNzAtFs6w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Despised by most beyond the school walls, he and those around him are all but prisoners as they attempt to learn control of the Gift. Worse, as Davian struggles with his lessons, he knows that there is further to fall if he cannot pass his final tests. \n\nBut when Davian discovers he has the ability to wield the forbidden power of the Augurs, he sets into motion a chain of events that will change everything.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">About Brandon Sanderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1394044556p3/38550.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">Brandon Sanderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
154,095
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14257202676705322510">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText14257202676705322510" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14257202676705322510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
